class="bday">1948-10-06</span>) </span>6 October 1948<span class="noprint ForceAgeToShow"> (age&#160;72)</span><br /><a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Political party</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Spouse(s)</th><td class="infobox-data">Collette McArdle</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Children</th><td class="infobox-data">1</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://sinnfein.ie/contents/20204">sinnfein<wbr />.ie<wbr />/contents<wbr />/20204</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Gerard Adams</b> (<a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>: <i lang="ga">Gear\xc3\xb3id Mac \xc3\x81dhaimh</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> born 6 October 1948) is an <a href="/wiki/Irish_republicanism" title="Irish republicanism">Irish republican</a> politician who was the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="President of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">president of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a> between 13 November 1983 and 10 February 2018, and served as a <a href="/wiki/Teachta_D%C3%A1la" title="Teachta D\xc3\xa1la">Teachta D\xc3\xa1la</a> (TD) for <a href="/wiki/Louth_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Louth (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Louth</a> from <a href="/wiki/2011_Irish_general_election" title="2011 Irish general election">2011</a> to <a href="/wiki/2020_Irish_general_election" title="2020 Irish general election">2020</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-oireachtas_db_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oireachtas_db-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-elecs_irl_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elecs_irl-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> From <a href="/wiki/1983_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1983 United Kingdom general election">1983</a> to <a href="/wiki/1992_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1992 United Kingdom general election">1992</a> and from <a href="/wiki/1997_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1997 United Kingdom general election">1997</a> to <a href="/wiki/2011_Belfast_West_by-election" title="2011 Belfast West by-election">2011</a>, he was an <a href="/wiki/Abstentionism" title="Abstentionism">abstentionist</a> <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament_(United_Kingdom)" title="Member of Parliament (United Kingdom)">Member of Parliament</a> (MP) of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">British Parliament</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Belfast West (UK Parliament constituency)">Belfast West constituency</a>.\n</p><p>In 1984, Adams was seriously wounded in an assassination attempt by several gunmen from the <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Defence_Association" title="Ulster Defence Association">Ulster Defence Association</a> (UDA), including <a href="/wiki/John_Gregg_(UDA)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Gregg (UDA)">John Gregg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> From the late 1980s onwards, he was an important figure in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_peace_process" title="Northern Ireland peace process">Northern Ireland peace process</a>, initially following contact by <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_and_Labour_Party" title="Social Democratic and Labour Party">Social Democratic and Labour Party</a> (SDLP) leader <a href="/wiki/John_Hume" title="John Hume">John Hume</a> and then subsequently with the <a href="/wiki/Irish_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish government">Irish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Her Majesty&#39;s Government">British</a> governments.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> He led Sinn F\xc3\xa9in to change its traditional policy of <a href="/wiki/Abstentionism" title="Abstentionism">abstentionism</a> towards the <a href="/wiki/Oireachtas" title="Oireachtas">Oireachtas</a>, the parliament of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>, in 1986; it later took seats in the <a href="/wiki/D%27Hondt_method" title="D&#39;Hondt method">power-sharing</a> <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly" title="Northern Ireland Assembly">Northern Ireland Assembly</a>. In 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Provisional Irish Republican Army">Provisional Irish Republican Army</a> (IRA) stated that its armed campaign was over and that it was exclusively committed to peaceful politics.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014, Adams was held for four days by the <a href="/wiki/Police_Service_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Police Service of Northern Ireland">Police Service of Northern Ireland</a> for questioning in connection with the abduction and <a href="/wiki/Murder_of_Jean_McConville" title="Murder of Jean McConville">murder of Jean McConville</a> in 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> He was freed without charge and a file was sent to the <a href="/wiki/Public_Prosecution_Service_for_Northern_Ireland" title="Public Prosecution Service for Northern Ireland">Public Prosecution Service</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> which later stated there was insufficient evidence to charge him,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> as had been expected since shortly after his release.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Insuff01_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Insuff01-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mirror-Insuff01_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mirror-Insuff01-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Adams announced in November 2017 that he would step down as leader of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in in 2018, and that he would not stand for re-election to his seat in the D\xc3\xa1il in the <a href="/wiki/2020_Irish_general_election" title="2020 Irish general election">2020 election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Retirement_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Retirement-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> He was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_McDonald" title="Mary Lou McDonald">Mary Lou McDonald</a> at a special <a href="/wiki/Ardfheis" title="Ardfheis">ardfheis</a> (party conference) on 10 February 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-IrishTimes2018-01-20a_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishTimes2018-01-20a-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Early_life"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Early href="#Rise_in_Sinn_F\xc3\xa9in"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Rise in Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#President_of_Sinn_F\xc3\xa9in"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">President of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#Voice_ban"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Voice ban</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Movement_into_mainstream_politics"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Movement into mainstream politics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Sinn_F\xc3\xa9in_in_government"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in in government</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Election_to_D\xc3\xa1il_\xc3\x89ireann"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Election to D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#End_of_Sinn_F\xc3\xa9in_presidency"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">End of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in presidency</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Personal_life"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Personal life</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Controversy"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Controversy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Media_portrayals"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Media portrayals</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Published_works"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Published works</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerry_Adams&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Adams was born in the <a href="/wiki/Springfield_Road#Ballymurphy_and_Whiterock" title="Springfield Road">Ballymurphy</a> district of <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a><sup id="cite_ref-bbcadams_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcadams-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> on 6 October 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> His parents, Anne (n\xc3\xa9e Hannaway) and <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Adams_Sr." title="Gerry Adams Sr.">Gerry Adams Sr.</a>, came from <a href="/wiki/Irish_republicanism" title="Irish republicanism">republican</a> backgrounds.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_adams_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica_adams-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> His grandfather, also named Gerry Adams, was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republican_Brotherhood" title="Irish Republican Brotherhood">Irish Republican Brotherhood</a> (IRB) during the <a href="/wiki/Irish_War_of_Independence" title="Irish War of Independence">Irish War of Independence</a>. Two of his uncles, Dominic and Patrick Adams, had been interned by the governments in Belfast and <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/J._Bowyer_Bell" title="J. Bowyer Bell">J. Bowyer Bell</a>\'s book <i>The Secret Army</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Bell states that Dominic was a senior figure in the IRA of the mid-1940s. Gerry Adams Sr. joined the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republican_Army_(1922%E2%80%931969)" title="Irish Republican Army (1922\xe2\x80\x931969)">IRA</a> at age 16. In 1942, he participated in an IRA ambush on a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Ulster_Constabulary" title="Royal Ulster Constabulary">Royal Ulster Constabulary</a> (RUC) patrol but was himself shot, arrested and sentenced to eight years\' imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcadams_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcadams-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Adams\'s maternal great-grandfather, Michael Hannaway, was also a member of the IRB during its <a href="/wiki/Fenian_Rising" title="Fenian Rising">bombing campaign in England in the 1860s and 1870s</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Michael\'s son, Billy, was election agent for <a href="/wiki/%C3%89amon_de_Valera" title="\xc3\x89amon de Valera">\xc3\x89amon de Valera</a> at the <a href="/wiki/1918_Irish_general_election" title="1918 Irish general election">1918 Irish general election</a> in <a href="/wiki/Belfast_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Belfast West (UK Parliament constituency)">West Belfast</a>. Adams attended <a href="/wiki/St_Finian%27s_Primary_School" title="St Finian&#39;s Primary School">St Finian\'s Primary School</a> on <a href="/wiki/Falls_Road,_Belfast" title="Falls Road, Belfast">Falls Road</a>, where he was taught by <a href="/wiki/Lasallian_educational_institutions" title="Lasallian educational institutions">La Salle brothers</a>. Having passed the <a href="/wiki/Eleven-plus" title="Eleven-plus">eleven-plus</a> exam in 1960, he attended <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_Christian_Brothers_Grammar_School" class="mw-redirect" title="St Mary&#39;s Christian Brothers Grammar School">St Mary\'s Christian Brothers Grammar School</a>. He left St Mary\'s with six <a href="/wiki/O-levels" class="mw-redirect" title="O-levels">O-levels</a> and became a bartender. He was increasingly involved in the <a href="/wiki/Republican_movement_(Ireland)" title="Republican movement (Ireland)">Irish republican movement</a>, joining <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fianna_%C3%89ireann" title="Fianna \xc3\x89ireann">Fianna \xc3\x89ireann</a> in 1964, after being radicalised by the Divis Street riots during <a href="/wiki/1964_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1964 United Kingdom general election">that year\'s general election</a> campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-EI_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EI-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_political_career">Early political career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerry_Adams&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early political career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gerry_Adams_Easter_Lily_Badge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gerry_Adams_Easter_Lily_Badge.jpg/170px-Gerry_Adams_Easter_Lily_Badge.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gerry_Adams_Easter_Lily_Badge.jpg/255px-Gerry_Adams_Easter_Lily_Badge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gerry_Adams_Easter_Lily_Badge.jpg/340px-Gerry_Adams_Easter_Lily_Badge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gerry_Adams_Easter_Lily_Badge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Adams wearing an <a href="/wiki/Easter_Lily_(badge)" title="Easter Lily (badge)">Easter Lily</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In the late 1960s, a <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_civil_rights_movement" title="Northern Ireland civil rights movement">civil rights campaign developed in Northern Ireland</a>. Adams was an active supporter and joined the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Civil_Rights_Association" title="Northern Ireland Civil Rights Association">Northern Ireland Civil Rights Association</a> in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-EI_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EI-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> However, the civil rights movement was met with violence from <a href="/wiki/Ulster_loyalism" title="Ulster loyalism">loyalist</a> counter-demonstrations and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Ulster_Constabulary" title="Royal Ulster Constabulary">Royal Ulster Constabulary</a>. In August 1969, the <a href="/wiki/1969_Northern_Ireland_riots" title="1969 Northern Ireland riots">Northern Ireland riots</a> resulted in violence in Belfast, <a href="/wiki/Derry" title="Derry">Derry</a> and elsewhere. British troops were called in at the request of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Government of Northern Ireland">Government of Northern Ireland</a>.\n</p><p>Adams was active in rioting at this time and later became involved in the republican movement. In August 1971, <a href="/wiki/Internment" title="Internment">internment</a> was reintroduced to Northern Ireland under the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Authorities_(Special_Powers)_Act_(Northern_Ireland)_1922" title="Civil Authorities (Special Powers) Act (Northern Ireland) 1922">Special Powers Act 1922</a>. Adams was interned in March 1972, on <a href="/wiki/HMS_Maidstone_(1937)" title="HMS Maidstone (1937)">HMS&#160;<i>Maidstone</i></a>, but on the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_IRA" class="mw-redirect" title="Provisional IRA">Provisional IRA</a>\'s insistence was released in June to take part in secret, but abortive talks in London.<sup id="cite_ref-EI_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EI-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The IRA negotiated a short-lived truce with the British government and an IRA delegation met with British Home Secretary <a href="/wiki/William_Whitelaw" class="mw-redirect" title="William Whitelaw">William Whitelaw</a> at <a href="/wiki/Cheyne_Walk" title="Cheyne Walk">Cheyne Walk</a> in Chelsea. The delegation included Adams, <a href="/wiki/Martin_McGuinness" title="Martin McGuinness">Martin McGuinness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sean_Mac_Stiofain" class="mw-redirect" title="Sean Mac Stiofain">Sean Mac Stiofain</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chief_of_Staff_of_the_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Chief of Staff of the Irish Republican Army">IRA Chief of Staff</a>), <a href="/wiki/Daithi_O%27Conaill" class="mw-redirect" title="Daithi O&#39;Conaill">Daithi O\'Conaill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seamus_Twomey" title="Seamus Twomey">Seamus Twomey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Bell" title="Ivor Bell">Ivor Bell</a> and Dublin solicitor <a href="/wiki/Myles_Shevlin" title="Myles Shevlin">Myles Shevlin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Adams was re-arrested in July 1973 and interned at the <a href="/wiki/Maze_(HM_Prison)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maze (HM Prison)">Maze prison</a>. After taking part in an IRA-organised escape attempt, he was sentenced to a period of imprisonment. During this time, he wrote articles in the paper <i><a href="/wiki/An_Phoblacht" title="An Phoblacht">An Phoblacht</a></i> under the by-line "Brownie", where he criticised the strategy and policy of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in president <a href="/wiki/Ruair%C3%AD_%C3%93_Br%C3%A1daigh" title="Ruair\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh">Ruair\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Billy_McKee" title="Billy McKee">Billy McKee</a>, the IRA\'s <a href="/wiki/Officer_commanding" title="Officer commanding">officer commanding</a> in Belfast. He was also highly critical of a decision taken by McKee to assassinate members of the rival <a href="/wiki/Official_IRA" class="mw-redirect" title="Official IRA">Official IRA</a>, who had been on ceasefire since 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-moloney_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moloney-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In 2020, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Supreme Court of the United Kingdom">UK Supreme Court</a> quashed Adams\' convictions for attempting to escape on Christmas Eve in 1973 and again in July 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/1981_Irish_hunger_strike" title="1981 Irish hunger strike">1981 hunger strike</a>, which saw the emergence of his party as a political force, Adams played an important policy-making role. In 1983, he was elected president of <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a> and became the first Sinn F\xc3\xa9in MP elected to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">British House of Commons</a> since <a href="/wiki/Philip_Clarke_(politician)" title="Philip Clarke (politician)">Phil Clarke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tom_Mitchell_(Irish_politician)" title="Tom Mitchell (Irish politician)">Tom Mitchell</a> in the mid-1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-EI_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EI-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Following his election as MP for <a href="/wiki/Belfast_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Belfast West (UK Parliament constituency)">Belfast West</a>, the British government lifted a ban on his travelling to Great Britain. In line with Sinn F\xc3\xa9in policy, he refused to take his seat in the House of Commons.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 14 March 1984 in central Belfast, Adams was seriously wounded in an assassination attempt when several <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Defence_Association" title="Ulster Defence Association">Ulster Defence Association</a> (UDA) gunmen fired about 20 shots into the car in which he was travelling. He was hit in the neck, shoulder and arm. He was rushed to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Victoria_Hospital,_Belfast" title="Royal Victoria Hospital, Belfast">Royal Victoria Hospital</a>, where he underwent surgery to remove three bullets. <a href="/wiki/John_Gregg_(UDA)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Gregg (UDA)">John Gregg</a> and his team were apprehended almost immediately by a <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> patrol that opened fire on them before ramming their car.<sup id="cite_ref-UDA129_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UDA129-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The attack had been known in advance by security forces due to a tip-off from informants within the UDA; Adams and his co-passengers had survived in part because <a href="/wiki/Royal_Ulster_Constabulary" title="Royal Ulster Constabulary">Royal Ulster Constabulary</a> officers, acting on the informants\' information, had replaced much of the ammunition in the UDA\'s Rathcoole weapons dump with low-velocity bullets.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Defence_Regiment" title="Ulster Defence Regiment">Ulster Defence Regiment</a> NCO subsequently received the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Gallantry_Medal" title="Queen&#39;s Gallantry Medal">Queen\'s Gallantry Medal</a> for chasing and arresting an assailant.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IRA_allegations">IRA allegations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerry_Adams&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: IRA allegations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Adams has stated repeatedly that he has never been a member of the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Provisional Irish Republican Army">Provisional Irish Republican Army</a> (IRA).<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> However, authors such as <a href="/wiki/Ed_Moloney" title="Ed Moloney">Ed Moloney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Taylor_(journalist)" title="Peter Taylor (journalist)">Peter Taylor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Urban" title="Mark Urban">Mark Urban</a> and historian <a href="/wiki/Richard_English" title="Richard English">Richard English</a> have all named Adams as part of the IRA leadership since the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Moloney and Taylor state Adams became the <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_Staff_of_the_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Chief of Staff of the Irish Republican Army">IRA\'s Chief of Staff</a> following the arrest of Seamus Twomey in early December 1977, remaining in the position until 18 February 1978 when he, along with twenty other republican suspects, was arrested following the <a href="/wiki/La_Mon_restaurant_bombing" title="La Mon restaurant bombing">La Mon restaurant bombing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> He was charged with IRA membership and remanded to <a href="/wiki/Crumlin_Road_Gaol" class="mw-redirect" title="Crumlin Road Gaol">Crumlin Road Gaol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> He was released seven months later when the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chief_Justice_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Lord Chief Justice of Northern Ireland">Lord Chief Justice of Northern Ireland</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Lowry,_Baron_Lowry" title="Robert Lowry, Baron Lowry">Robert Lowry</a> ruled there was insufficient evidence to proceed with the prosecution.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Moloney and English state Adams had been a member of the <a href="/wiki/IRA_Army_Council" title="IRA Army Council">IRA Army Council</a> since 1977, remaining a member until 2005 according to Irish <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Justice_(Ireland)" title="Minister for Justice (Ireland)">Minister for Justice, Equality and Law Reform</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_McDowell_(politician)" title="Michael McDowell (politician)">Michael McDowell</a>. <sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_arrest">2014 arrest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerry_Adams&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2014 arrest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 30 April 2014, Adams was arrested by detectives from the <a href="/wiki/Police_Service_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Police Service of Northern Ireland">Police Service of Northern Ireland</a> (PSNI) Serious Crime Branch, under the <a href="/wiki/Terrorism_Act_2000" title="Terrorism Act 2000">Terrorism Act 2000</a>, in connection with the <a href="/wiki/Murder_of_Jean_McConville" title="Murder of Jean McConville">murder of Jean McConville</a> in 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> He had previously voluntarily arranged to be interviewed by police regarding the matter,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> and maintained he had no involvement.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_McConville_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_McConville-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Fellow Sinn F\xc3\xa9in politician <a href="/wiki/Alex_Maskey" title="Alex Maskey">Alex Maskey</a> claimed that the timing of the arrest, "three weeks into an election", was evidence of a "political agenda [...] a negative agenda" by the PSNI.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Jean McConville\'s family had campaigned for the arrest of Adams over the murder.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Jean McConville\'s son Michael said that his family did not think the arrest of Adams would ever happen, but were "quite glad" that the arrest took place. Adams was released without charge after four days in custody and it was decided to send a file to the <a href="/wiki/Public_Prosecution_Service_for_Northern_Ireland" title="Public Prosecution Service for Northern Ireland">Public Prosecution Service</a>, which would decide if criminal charges should be brought.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Adams_released_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adams_released-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At a press conference after his release, Adams also criticised the timing of his arrest, while reiterating Sinn F\xc3\xa9in\'s support for the PSNI and saying: "The IRA is gone. It is finished".<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Adams has denied that he had any involvement in the murder or was ever a member of the IRA,<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_McConville_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_McConville-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Deny01_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Deny01-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> and has said the allegations against him came from "enemies of the peace process".<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> On 29 September 2015 the Public Prosecution Service announced Adams would not face charges, due to insufficient evidence,<sup id="cite_ref-G2015_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G2015-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> as had been expected ever since a <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> report dated 6 May 2014 (2 days after the BBC reported his release),<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Insuff01_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Insuff01-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> which was widely repeated elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-Mirror-Insuff01_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mirror-Insuff01-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Rise_in_Sinn_F.C3.A9in"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_in_Sinn_F\xc3\xa9in">Rise in Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerry_Adams&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Rise in Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gerry_Adams_reading_into_mic.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gerry_Adams_reading_into_mic.jpg/220px-Gerry_Adams_reading_into_mic.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gerry_Adams_reading_into_mic.jpg/330px-Gerry_Adams_reading_into_mic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gerry_Adams_reading_into_mic.jpg/440px-Gerry_Adams_reading_into_mic.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gerry_Adams_reading_into_mic.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Adams at a commemoration in <a href="/wiki/Fermanagh" title="Fermanagh">Fermanagh</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1978, Adams became joint vice-president of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in and a key figure in directing a challenge to the Sinn F\xc3\xa9in leadership of President <a href="/wiki/Ruair%C3%AD_%C3%93_Br%C3%A1daigh" title="Ruair\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh">Ruair\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh</a> and joint vice-president <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1ith%C3%AD_%C3%93_Conaill" title="D\xc3\xa1ith\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 Conaill">D\xc3\xa1ith\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 Conaill</a>. The 1975 IRA-British truce is often viewed as the event that began the challenge to the original Provisional Sinn F\xc3\xa9in leadership, which was dominated by southerners like \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh and \xc3\x93 Conaill.\n</p><p>One of the reasons that the Provisional IRA and Provisional Sinn F\xc3\xa9in were founded, in December 1969 and January 1970, respectively, was that people like \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh, \xc3\x93 Conaill and McKee opposed participation in constitutional politics. The other reason was the failure of the <a href="/wiki/Cathal_Goulding" title="Cathal Goulding">Cathal Goulding</a> leadership to provide for the defence of <a href="/wiki/Irish_nationalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish nationalist">Irish nationalist</a> areas during the <a href="/wiki/1969_Northern_Ireland_riots" title="1969 Northern Ireland riots">1969 Northern Ireland riots</a>. When, at the December 1969 IRA convention and the January 1970 Sinn F\xc3\xa9in Ard Fheis, the delegates voted to participate in the Dublin (Leinster House), Belfast (Stormont) and London (Westminster) parliaments, the organisations split. Adams, who had joined the republican movement in the early 1960s, sided with the Provisionals.\n</p><p>In Long Kesh in the mid-1970s, writing under the pseudonym "Brownie" in <i><a href="/wiki/Republican_News" title="Republican News">Republican News</a></i>, Adams called for increased political activity among republicans, especially at local level.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The call resonated with younger Northern people, many of whom had been active in the Provisional IRA but few of whom had been active in Sinn F\xc3\xa9in. In 1977, Adams and <a href="/wiki/Danny_Morrison_(Irish_republican)" title="Danny Morrison (Irish republican)">Danny Morrison</a> drafted the address of Jimmy Drumm at the annual <a href="/wiki/Wolfe_Tone" title="Wolfe Tone">Wolfe Tone</a> commemoration at <a href="/wiki/Bodenstown" class="mw-redirect" title="Bodenstown">Bodenstown</a>. The address was viewed as watershed in that Drumm acknowledged that the war would be a long one and that success depended on political activity that would complement the IRA\'s armed campaign. For some,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (August 2010)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> this wedding of politics and armed struggle culminated in Danny Morrison\'s statement at the 1981 Sinn F\xc3\xa9in Ard Fheis in which he asked "<a href="/wiki/Armalite_and_ballot_box_strategy" title="Armalite and ballot box strategy">Who here really believes we can win the war through the ballot box? But will anyone here object if, with a ballot paper in one hand and the Armalite in the other, we take power in Ireland</a>?" For others, however, the call to link political activity with armed struggle had already been defined in Sinn F\xc3\xa9in policy and in the presidential addresses of Ruair\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh, but this had not resonated with young Northerners.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Even after the election of <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Sands" title="Bobby Sands">Bobby Sands</a> as MP for <a href="/wiki/Fermanagh_and_South_Tyrone_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Fermanagh and South Tyrone (UK Parliament constituency)">Fermanagh and South Tyrone</a>, a part of the mass mobilisation associated with the <a href="/wiki/1981_Irish_Hunger_Strike" class="mw-redirect" title="1981 Irish Hunger Strike">1981 Irish Hunger Strike</a> by republican prisoners in the <a href="/wiki/HM_Prison_Maze#H-Blocks" title="HM Prison Maze">H blocks</a> of the <a href="/wiki/HM_Prison_Maze" title="HM Prison Maze">Maze Prison</a> (known as Long Kesh by republicans), Adams was cautious that the level of political involvement by Sinn F\xc3\xa9in could lead to electoral embarrassment. <a href="/wiki/Charles_Haughey" title="Charles Haughey">Charles Haughey</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>, called <a href="/wiki/1981_Irish_general_election" title="1981 Irish general election">an election</a> for June 1981. At an Ard Chomhairle meeting, Adams recommended that they contest only four constituencies which were in border counties. Instead, H-Block/Armagh candidates contested nine constituencies and elected two TDs. This, along with the election of Sands, was a precursor to an electoral breakthrough in <a href="/wiki/1982_Northern_Ireland_Assembly_election" title="1982 Northern Ireland Assembly election">elections in 1982</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly_(1982)" title="Northern Ireland Assembly (1982)">1982 Northern Ireland Assembly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Adams, Danny Morrison, <a href="/wiki/Martin_McGuinness" title="Martin McGuinness">Martin McGuinness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_McAllister_(Irish_republican)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jim McAllister (Irish republican)">Jim McAllister</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Owen_Carron" title="Owen Carron">Owen Carron</a> were elected as abstentionists. The <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_and_Labour_Party" title="Social Democratic and Labour Party">Social Democratic and Labour Party</a> (SDLP) had announced before the election that it would not take any seats and so its 14 elected representatives also abstained from participating in the Assembly and it was a failure. The 1982 election was followed by the <a href="/wiki/1983_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1983 United Kingdom general election">1983 Westminster election</a>, in which Sinn F\xc3\xa9in\'s vote increased and Adams was elected, as an abstentionist, as MP for Belfast West. It was in 1983 that Ruair\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh resigned as President of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in and was succeeded by Adams.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="President_of_Sinn_F.C3.A9in"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="President_of_Sinn_F\xc3\xa9in">President of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerry_Adams&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: President of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Many republicans had long claimed that the only legitimate Irish state was the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republic" title="Irish Republic">Irish Republic</a> declared in the <a href="/wiki/Proclamation_of_the_Irish_Republic" title="Proclamation of the Irish Republic">1916 Proclamation of the Republic</a>. In their view, the legitimate government was the <a href="/wiki/IRA_Army_Council" title="IRA Army Council">IRA Army Council</a>, which had been vested with the authority of that Republic in 1938 (prior to the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>) by the last remaining anti-<a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish_Treaty" title="Anglo-Irish Treaty">Treaty</a> deputies of the <a href="/wiki/Second_D%C3%A1il" title="Second D\xc3\xa1il">Second D\xc3\xa1il</a>. In his 2005 speech to the Sinn F\xc3\xa9in <a href="/wiki/Ard_Fheis" class="mw-redirect" title="Ard Fheis">Ard Fheis</a> in Dublin, Adams explicitly rejected this view. "But we refuse to criminalise those who break the law in pursuit of legitimate political objectives. ... Sinn F\xc3\xa9in is accused of recognising the Army Council of the IRA as the legitimate government of this island. That is not the case. [We] do not believe that the Army Council is the government of Ireland. Such a government will only exist when all the people of this island elect it. Does Sinn F\xc3\xa9in accept the institutions of this state as the legitimate institutions of this state? Of course we do."<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As a result of this non-recognition, Sinn F\xc3\xa9in had abstained from taking any of the seats they won in the British or Irish parliaments. At its 1986 Ard Fheis, Sinn F\xc3\xa9in delegates passed a resolution to amend the rules and constitution that would allow its members to sit in the Dublin parliament (<a href="/wiki/Leinster_House" title="Leinster House">Leinster House</a>). At this, Ruair\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh led a small walkout, just as he and Sean Mac Stiofain had done sixteen years earlier with the creation of Provisional Sinn F\xc3\xa9in.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> This minority, which rejected dropping the policy of <a href="/wiki/Abstentionism" title="Abstentionism">abstentionism</a>, now distinguishes itself from Sinn F\xc3\xa9in by using the name <a href="/wiki/Republican_Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Republican Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">Republican Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a> (or Sinn F\xc3\xa9in Poblachtach), and maintains that they are the true Sinn F\xc3\xa9in.\n</p><p>Adams\' leadership of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in was supported by a Northern-based cadre that included people like <a href="/wiki/Danny_Morrison_(Irish_republican)" title="Danny Morrison (Irish republican)">Danny Morrison</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martin_McGuinness" title="Martin McGuinness">Martin McGuinness</a>. Over time, Adams and others pointed to republican electoral successes in the early and mid-1980s, when hunger strikers <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Sands" title="Bobby Sands">Bobby Sands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kieran_Doherty_(hunger_striker)" title="Kieran Doherty (hunger striker)">Kieran Doherty</a> were elected to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">British House of Commons</a> and <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_%C3%89ireann" title="D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann">D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</a> respectively, and they advocated that Sinn F\xc3\xa9in become increasingly political and base its influence on electoral politics rather than paramilitarism. The electoral effects of this strategy were shown later by the election of Adams and McGuinness to the House of Commons.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Voice_ban">Voice ban</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerry_Adams&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Voice ban">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Adams\'s prominence as an Irish republican leader was increased by the <a href="/wiki/1988%E2%80%9394_British_broadcasting_voice_restrictions" class="mw-redirect" title="1988\xe2\x80\x9394 British broadcasting voice restrictions">1988\xe2\x80\x9394 British broadcasting voice restrictions</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> which were imposed by British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> to "starve the terrorist and the hijacker of the oxygen of publicity on which they depend".<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Thatcher was moved to act after BBC interviews of <a href="/wiki/Martin_McGuinness" title="Martin McGuinness">Martin McGuinness</a> and Adams had been the focus of <a href="/wiki/After_Dark_(TV_series)#Gerry_Adams" class="mw-redirect" title="After Dark (TV series)">a row over an edition</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/After_Dark_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="After Dark (TV series)">After Dark</a></i>, a proposed <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a> discussion programme which in the event was never made.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> While the ban covered 11 Irish political parties and paramilitary organisations, in practice it mostly affected Sinn F\xc3\xa9in, the most prominent of these bodies.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A similar ban, known as <a href="/wiki/Censorship_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland#The_Troubles" title="Censorship in the Republic of Ireland">Section 31</a>, had been law in the Republic of Ireland since the 1970s. However, media outlets soon found ways around the bans. In the UK, this was initially by the use of subtitles, but later and more often by an actor reading words accompanied by video footage of the banned person speaking. Actors who voiced Adams included <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Rea" title="Stephen Rea">Stephen Rea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Loughran" title="Paul Loughran">Paul Loughran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> This loophole could not be used in the Republic, as word-for-word broadcasts were not allowed.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Instead, the banned speaker\'s words were summarised by the newsreader, over video of them speaking.\n</p><p>These bans were lampooned in cartoons and satirical TV shows, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Spitting_Image" title="Spitting Image">Spitting Image</a></i>, and in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Day_Today" title="The Day Today">The Day Today</a></i>, and were criticised by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a> organisations and media personalities, including BBC Director General <a href="/wiki/John_Birt" class="mw-redirect" title="John Birt">John Birt</a> and BBC foreign editor <a href="/wiki/John_Simpson_(journalist)" title="John Simpson (journalist)">John Simpson</a>. The Republic\'s ban was allowed to lapse in January 1994, and the British ban was lifted by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Major" title="John Major">John Major</a> in September.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Movement_into_mainstream_politics">Movement into mainstream politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerry_Adams&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Movement into mainstream politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Bill_Clinton_and_Gerry_Adams.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/President_Bill_Clinton_and_Gerry_Adams.jpg/220px-President_Bill_Clinton_and_Gerry_Adams.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/President_Bill_Clinton_and_Gerry_Adams.jpg/330px-President_Bill_Clinton_and_Gerry_Adams.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/President_Bill_Clinton_and_Gerry_Adams.jpg/440px-President_Bill_Clinton_and_Gerry_Adams.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5582" data-file-height="3739" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Bill_Clinton_and_Gerry_Adams.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Adams with <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> in 1995</div></div></div>\n<p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in continued its policy of refusing to sit in the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Westminster Parliament</a> after Adams won the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Belfast West (UK Parliament constituency)">Belfast West</a> constituency. He lost his seat to <a href="/wiki/Joe_Hendron" title="Joe Hendron">Joe Hendron</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_and_Labour_Party" title="Social Democratic and Labour Party">Social Democratic and Labour Party</a> (SDLP) in the <a href="/wiki/1992_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1992 United Kingdom general election">1992 general election</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> regaining it at the following <a href="/wiki/1997_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1997 United Kingdom general election">1997 election</a>. Under Adams, Sinn F\xc3\xa9in moved away from being a political voice of the Provisional IRA to becoming a professionally organised political party in both <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> and the Republic of Ireland.\n</p><p>SDLP leader <a href="/wiki/John_Hume" title="John Hume">John Hume</a> identified the possibility that a negotiated settlement might be possible and began secret talks with Adams in 1988. These discussions led to unofficial contacts with the British <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Office" title="Northern Ireland Office">Northern Ireland Office</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Northern_Ireland" title="Secretary of State for Northern Ireland">Secretary of State for Northern Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Brooke" class="mw-redirect" title="Peter Brooke">Peter Brooke</a>, and with the government of the Republic under <a href="/wiki/Charles_Haughey" title="Charles Haughey">Charles Haughey</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 although both governments maintained in public that they would not negotiate with terrorists.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> These talks provided the groundwork for what was later to be the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast Agreement">Belfast Agreement</a>, preceded by the milestone <a href="/wiki/Downing_Street_Declaration" title="Downing Street Declaration">Downing Street Declaration</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Framework_Document" class="mw-redirect" title="Joint Framework Document">Joint Framework Document</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>These negotiations led to the IRA ceasefire in August 1994. <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a> <a href="/wiki/Albert_Reynolds" title="Albert Reynolds">Albert Reynolds</a>, who had replaced Haughey and who had played a key role in the Hume/Adams dialogue through his Special Advisor <a href="/wiki/Martin_Mansergh" title="Martin Mansergh">Martin Mansergh</a>, regarded the ceasefire as permanent. However, the slow pace of developments contributed in part to the (wider) political difficulties of the British government of <a href="/wiki/John_Major" title="John Major">John Major</a>. His consequent reliance on <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Unionist_Party" title="Ulster Unionist Party">Ulster Unionist Party</a> (UUP) votes in the House of Commons led to him agreeing with the UUP demand to exclude Sinn F\xc3\xa9in from talks until the IRA had <a href="/wiki/Decommissioning_in_Northern_Ireland" title="Decommissioning in Northern Ireland">decommissioned its weapons</a>. Sinn F\xc3\xa9in\'s exclusion led the IRA to end its ceasefire and resume its campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/1997_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1997 United Kingdom general election">1997 United Kingdom general election</a>, the new Labour government had a majority in the House of Commons and was not reliant on unionist votes. The subsequent dropping of the insistence led to another IRA ceasefire, as part of the negotiations strategy, which saw teams from the British and Irish governments, the UUP, the SDLP, Sinn F\xc3\xa9in, and representatives of loyalist paramilitary organisations, under the chairmanship of former United States Senator <a href="/wiki/George_J._Mitchell" title="George J. Mitchell">George Mitchell</a>, produce the <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement" title="Good Friday Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a> in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_adams_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica_adams-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Under the Agreement, structures were created reflecting the Irish and British identities of the people of Ireland, creating a <a href="/wiki/British-Irish_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="British-Irish Council">British-Irish Council</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly" title="Northern Ireland Assembly">Northern Ireland Legislative Assembly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Articles_2_and_3" class="mw-redirect" title="Articles 2 and 3">Articles 2 and 3</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Constitution of Ireland">Republic\'s constitution</a>, which claimed sovereignty over all of Ireland, were reworded, and a power-sharing Executive Committee was provided for. As part of their deal, Sinn F\xc3\xa9in agreed to abandon its abstentionist policy regarding a "six-county parliament", as a result taking seats in the new <a href="/wiki/Parliament_Buildings_(Northern_Ireland)" title="Parliament Buildings (Northern Ireland)">Stormont</a>-based Assembly and running the education and health and social services ministries in the power-sharing government.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Sinn_F.C3.A9in_in_government"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sinn_F\xc3\xa9in_in_government">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in in government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerry_Adams&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sinn F\xc3\xa9in in government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:George_W._Bush,_Peter_King,_and_Gerry_Adams.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/George_W._Bush%2C_Peter_King%2C_and_Gerry_Adams.jpg/220px-George_W._Bush%2C_Peter_King%2C_and_Gerry_Adams.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/George_W._Bush%2C_Peter_King%2C_and_Gerry_Adams.jpg/330px-George_W._Bush%2C_Peter_King%2C_and_Gerry_Adams.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/00/George_W._Bush%2C_Peter_King%2C_and_Gerry_Adams.jpg 2x" data-file-width="392" data-file-height="403" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:George_W._Bush,_Peter_King,_and_Gerry_Adams.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Adams with <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_T._King" title="Peter T. King">Peter King</a> in 2001</div></div></div>\n<p>On 15 August 1998, four months after the signing of the Good Friday Agreement, the <a href="/wiki/Omagh_bombing" title="Omagh bombing">Omagh bombing</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Real_IRA" class="mw-redirect" title="Real IRA">Real IRA</a>, killed 29 people and injured 220, from many communities. Adams said in reaction to the bombing "I am totally horrified by this action. I condemn it without any equivocation whatsoever."<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Prior to this, Adams had not used the word "condemn" in relation to IRA or their splinter groups\' actions.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When Sinn F\xc3\xa9in came to nominate its two ministers to the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Executive" title="Northern Ireland Executive">Northern Ireland Executive</a>, for tactical reasons the party, like the SDLP and the DUP, chose not to include its leader among its ministers. When later the SDLP chose a new leader, it selected one of its ministers, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Durkan" title="Mark Durkan">Mark Durkan</a>, who then opted to remain in the committee.\n</p><p>Adams was re-elected to the Northern Ireland Assembly on 8 March 2007, and on 26 March 2007, he met with DUP leader <a href="/wiki/Ian_Paisley" title="Ian Paisley">Ian Paisley</a> face-to-face for the first time. These talks led to the <a href="/wiki/St_Andrews_Agreement" title="St Andrews Agreement">St Andrews Agreement</a>, which brought about the return of the power-sharing Executive in Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2009, Adams attended the United States presidential <a href="/wiki/First_inauguration_of_Barack_Obama" title="First inauguration of Barack Obama">inauguration of Barack Obama</a> as a guest of US Congressman <a href="/wiki/Richard_Neal" title="Richard Neal">Richard Neal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Election_to_D.C3.A1il_.C3.89ireann"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Election_to_D\xc3\xa1il_\xc3\x89ireann">Election to D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerry_Adams&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Election to D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Euclid_Tsakalotos_Gerry_Adams_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Euclid_Tsakalotos_Gerry_Adams_2015.jpg/220px-Euclid_Tsakalotos_Gerry_Adams_2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Euclid_Tsakalotos_Gerry_Adams_2015.jpg/330px-Euclid_Tsakalotos_Gerry_Adams_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Euclid_Tsakalotos_Gerry_Adams_2015.jpg/440px-Euclid_Tsakalotos_Gerry_Adams_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Euclid_Tsakalotos_Gerry_Adams_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gerry Adams with <a href="/wiki/Euclid_Tsakalotos" title="Euclid Tsakalotos">Euclid Tsakalotos</a> at the Sinn F\xc3\xa9in ardfheis in March 2015</div></div></div>\n<p>On 6 May 2010, Adams was re-elected as MP for West Belfast, garnering 71.1% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Adams announced that he would be seeking election as a <a href="/wiki/Teachta_D%C3%A1la" title="Teachta D\xc3\xa1la">TD</a> (member of Irish Parliament) for the constituency of <a href="/wiki/Louth_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Louth (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Louth</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2011_Irish_general_election" title="2011 Irish general election">2011 Irish general election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> He subsequently resigned his West Belfast <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly" title="Northern Ireland Assembly">Assembly</a> seat on 7 December 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the announcement of the <a href="/wiki/2011_Irish_general_election" title="2011 Irish general election">2011 Irish general election</a>, Adams <a href="/wiki/Resignation_from_the_British_House_of_Commons" title="Resignation from the British House of Commons">resigned his seat at the House of Commons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> He was elected to the D\xc3\xa1il, topping the Louth constituency poll with 15,072 (21.7%) first preference votes.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> He succeeded <a href="/wiki/Caoimhgh%C3%ADn_%C3%93_Caol%C3%A1in" title="Caoimhgh\xc3\xadn \xc3\x93 Caol\xc3\xa1in">Caoimhgh\xc3\xadn \xc3\x93 Caol\xc3\xa1in</a> as Sinn F\xc3\xa9in parliamentary leader in D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 19 May 2015, while on an official royal trip to Ireland, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Charles" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Charles">Prince Charles</a> shook Adams\' hand in what was described as a highly symbolic gesture of reconciliation. The meeting, described as "historic", took place in Galway.<sup id="cite_ref-guardianmay19_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardianmay19-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2017, Adams said he would allow his name to go forward for a one-year term as president of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in at the November <a href="/wiki/Ardfheis" title="Ardfheis">ardfheis</a>, at which point Sinn F\xc3\xa9in would begin a "planned process of generational change, including [Adams\'] own future intentions". This resulted in speculation in the Irish and British media that Adams was preparing to stand down as party leader, and that he might run for <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ireland" title="President of Ireland">President of Ireland</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2018_Irish_presidential_election" title="2018 Irish presidential election">next election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> At the ardfheis on 18 November, Adams was re-elected for another year as party president, but announced that he would step down at some point in 2018, and would not seek re-election as TD for Louth.<sup id="cite_ref-Retirement_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Retirement-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="End_of_Sinn_F.C3.A9in_presidency"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_Sinn_F\xc3\xa9in_presidency">End of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in presidency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerry_Adams&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: End of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in presidency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Adams\' presidency of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in ended on 10 February 2018, with his stepping down, and the election of <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_McDonald" title="Mary Lou McDonald">Mary Lou McDonald</a> as the party\'s new president.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 13 July 2018, a home-made bomb was thrown at Adams\' home in West Belfast, damaging a car parked in his driveway. Adams escaped injury and claimed that his two grandchildren were standing in the driveway only 10 minutes before the blast. Another bomb was set off that same evening at the nearby home of former IRA <a href="/wiki/Volunteer_(Irish_republican)" title="Volunteer (Irish republican)">volunteer</a> and Sinn F\xc3\xa9in official <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Storey" title="Bobby Storey">Bobby Storey</a>. In a press conference the following day, Adams said he thought the attacks were linked to the <a href="/wiki/2018_Derry_riots" title="2018 Derry riots">riots in Derry</a>, and asked that those responsible "come and sit down" and "give us the rationale for this action".<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerry_Adams&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 1971, Adams married Collette McArdle.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> They have a son named Gearoid (born 1973),<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> who has played <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_football" title="Gaelic football">Gaelic football</a> for <a href="/wiki/Antrim_GAA" title="Antrim GAA">Antrim GAA</a> senior men\'s team and became its assistant manager in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2013, Adams\' brother Liam <a href="/wiki/Public_Prosecution_Service_of_Northern_Ireland_v._Liam_Adams" title="Public Prosecution Service of Northern Ireland v. Liam Adams">was found guilty</a> of 10 offences, including rape and gross indecency committed against his own daughter.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-news-verdict_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-news-verdict-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> When the allegations of abuse were first made public in a 2009 <a href="/wiki/UTV_(TV_channel)" title="UTV (TV channel)">UTV</a> programme, Adams subsequently alleged that <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Adams_Sr." title="Gerry Adams Sr.">his own father</a> had subjected family members to <a href="/wiki/Emotional_abuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Emotional abuse">emotional</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physical_abuse" title="Physical abuse">physical</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abuse" title="Sexual abuse">sexual abuse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> On 27 November 2013, Liam was jailed for 16 years.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">Controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerry_Adams&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>On 1 May 2016, Adams sparked controversy by <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">tweeting</a>, "Watching <i><a href="/wiki/Django_Unchained" title="Django Unchained">Django Unchained</a></i>-A <a href="/wiki/White_nigger" title="White nigger">Ballymurphy Nigger</a>!"<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The tweet was criticised and subsequently deleted, with Adams apologising for the use of "<a href="/wiki/Nigger" title="Nigger">nigger</a>" the next day at Sinn F\xc3\xa9in\'s Connolly House headquarter in Belfast. The tweet was widely reported in Irish,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> British,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> and American media.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Adams said, "I stand over the context and main point of my tweet, which were the parallels between people in struggle. Like African Americans, Irish nationalists were denied basic rights. I have long been inspired by <a href="/wiki/Harriet_Tubman" title="Harriet Tubman">Harriet Tubman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rosa_Parks" title="Rosa Parks">Rosa Parks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King" class="mw-redirect" title="Martin Luther King">Martin Luther King</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_X" title="Malcolm X">Malcolm X</a>, who stood up for themselves and for justice."<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> On 4 May, he said, "The whole thing was to make a political point. If I had left that word out, would the tweet have gotten any attention? [...] I was paralleling the experiences of the Irish, not just in recent times but through the <a href="/wiki/Penal_colony" title="Penal colony">penal</a> days when the Irish were sold as slaves, through the <a href="/wiki/Cromwellian_conquest_of_Ireland" title="Cromwellian conquest of Ireland">Cromwellian</a> period."<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> He was criticised for perpetrating the <a href="/wiki/Irish_slaves_myth" title="Irish slaves myth">Irish slaves myth</a>, which falsely equates the <a href="/wiki/Indentured_servitude" title="Indentured servitude">indentured servitude</a> of the Irish with the <a href="/wiki/Chattel_slavery" class="mw-redirect" title="Chattel slavery">chattel slavery</a> of African Americans.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_portrayals">Media portrayals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerry_Adams&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Media portrayals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Adams has been portrayed in a number of films, TV series, and books:\n</p>\n<ul><li>1999 \xe2\x80\x93 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Marching_Season" title="The Marching Season">The Marching Season</a></i>, a spy fiction novel by <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Silva_(novelist)" title="Daniel Silva (novelist)">Daniel Silva</a>.</li>\n<li>2004 \xe2\x80\x93 film <i><a href="/wiki/Omagh_(film)" title="Omagh (film)">Omagh</a></i>, with actor <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Ryan" title="Jonathan Ryan">Jonathan Ryan</a>, a dramatisation of the 1998 <a href="/wiki/Omagh_bombing" title="Omagh bombing">Omagh bombing</a> and its aftermath.</li>\n<li>2010 \xe2\x80\x93 TV film <i><a href="/wiki/Mo_(2010_film)" title="Mo (2010 film)">Mo</a></i>, with actor <a href="/wiki/John_Lynch_(actor)" title="John Lynch (actor)">John Lynch</a>, the story of <a href="/wiki/Mo_Mowlam" title="Mo Mowlam">Mo Mowlam</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement" title="Good Friday Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a>.</li>\n<li>2012 \xe2\x80\x93 <i>The Cold Cold Ground</i>, a crime novel by <a href="/wiki/Adrian_McKinty" title="Adrian McKinty">Adrian McKinty</a>; Adams is interviewed by the book\'s main character after an associate is found murdered.</li>\n<li>2016 \xe2\x80\x93 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Journey_(2016_film)" title="The Journey (2016 film)">The Journey</a></i>, with actor <a href="/wiki/Ian_Beattie" title="Ian Beattie">Ian Beattie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2017 \xe2\x80\x93 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Foreigner_(2017_film)" title="The Foreigner (2017 film)">The Foreigner</a></i>, with actor <a href="/wiki/Pierce_Brosnan" title="Pierce Brosnan">Pierce Brosnan</a> playing a former IRA leader who resembles Adams.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Published_works">Published works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span Irish Voice: The Quest for Peace</i></li>\n<li><i>Cage Eleven</i>, 1990, Brandon Books, <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r999302996">.mw-parser-output Brandon Books, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a
